### Post by TravisNewman on 2005-04-12
My machine is Eniac, when I got my Mac I called it Univac. When my fiancee and I moved in together, she thought it'd be funny to call hers Abacus, because her computer is so slow.

Eniac and Univac were two of the first major computer landmarks, and an abacus, for those who don't know, is a pre-electricity way of adding without doing it in your head or on paper. With sticks and beads and such

---

### Post by dare2dreamer on 2005-04-12
While the reasons for it are long and sordid, my current naming convention consists of somehow-relevant female mythological beings whose names begin with the letter "E".

So, with a little work we have:

echo - The jukebox, named from Greek myth.
evaki - My desktop, named for a South American Indian Goddess of Night and Day.
eve - A fileserver, named because she serves every network type including apple.
erzulie - Primary laptop, named for a Vodoun Loa of lust. (known for getting around.)

I'm thinking of eventually redoing my naming scheme so that all my machines are named for female supervillain sidekicks, just because I'm amused with the idea of calling my main machines harley and mercy.

Yes, my girlfriend thinks I'm weird too. Of course this is coming from a woman in possession of a laptop named after a stuffed animal.

### Post by NeoSNightmarE on 2005-07-31
Mine has the name G14. There's a story to go with it but I'll keep it short. When I was living in NYC, I was in trouble for something computer related with the FBI and they were investigating and what have you. This was back in 2000 btw, and they took my computer that was running Debian at the time. The reason it got the name though was because the agent that I was talking to had the rank of G14...or that's what he told me. Since then I've been using that when naming a computer anywhere. Just thought I would share the history too ;)

### Post by jouni on 2005-09-04
My desktop is called vaino and my laptop hella. This is a somewhat complicated linguistic joke: "Väinö" and "Hellä" are Finnish given names, but if you remove the umlauts, as you often have to do when dealing with computers, you get the words "vaino" (which means persecution or oppression) and "hella" (cooking stove).

### Post by lcg on 2005-11-30

Because of that little story, it is IMO especially funny to give that name to IBM computers.

### Post by curuxz on 2005-12-06
How the names came about are long stories, but the main reason for naming them is to confuse people browsing my network.

Primary PC is always named : CuruXz (hence my username)
Its slave laptop, that always sits next to it: Triax
finaly the one in my room for multimedia is: Enradi

To this day Curuxz is on its 6th incarnation, there have been 2 systems to bare the name Triax and 3 Enradi's since I started building systems. All run ubuntu, keeping the name the same for pc's doing the same job helps me know what backups im looking at by hostname. Also I once had Kobos as the name of a firewall server.

Its a good policy, treating them like pets mean you care for them....and dont  abuse them by installing windoze.

### Post by almahtar on 2005-12-11
[QUOTE=Claark]What an intresting thread.  I'll contribute.

I do web programing on an automated pharmacy ordering, sorting and shipping system.  I called it called BluePill[/QUOTE]
What? Why not red pill?  You telling me you'd prefer escape to the truth? :-p (J/k, of course).

I like to get creative with my computer names.

**Zomb0r** - a hastily scrapped together computer I never bothered putting the case covers on.
**Biotch** - network file server and jukebox
**almahtar** - my faithful old Athlon 550 I've had since 1999.  Almahtar is the elvish translation of my real name (Jonathan Mark), which means (loosely) "Blessed warrior."  I came up with it before LotR was such a mainstream influence, and it's proven to be a great screenname.
**Almahtarphoenix** - Almahtar's replacement when I flashed its bios unsuccessfully and ruined it.
**Santa** - Biotch's replacement which also ran a deditcated game server.  It was such a benevolent machine, always giving and never recieving, so it was named Santa.
**Zao** - Old Greek for "Alive."  The machine I hosted my CS381 group's CVS repository on.
**Dragonfly** - my only currently operational machine, a laptop.  It's zippy and portable, but more importantly "dragonfly" and "firefly" have been very symbolic of the similarities and differences between me and my (pseudo) girlfriend, respectively.

---

### Post by Dr. Nick on 2005-12-17
[quote=0okami]Is it possible to change the machine's name without affecting anything? 
I might be renaming my machine to Cerberus or Cerberos or Kerberos (for kubuntu) hehe

Cerebus was the three headed dog of Haydes. After tonight, i will be adding a third monitor to my setup.[/quote]

You can change the machines name with minimal effect. It depends on your network setup. 

A overly simple but practical way to tell
If you ever need to know your current hostname for usage on your network then it will have an effect
If you dont have a network that you use or you dont need to know the name to connect to it from the lan then you can change it without a problem.


I call my laptop ubuntu since I didnt name it on install, My laptop is springfield after the simpsons, I am going to rename my desktop shelbyville.

### Post by Tichondrius on 2006-02-01
I hope you people realize there is a practical purpose to naming computers - so that you can easily refer to them when you have multiple computers on your network. We're not doing this as a hobby or cause we have nothing better to do. And btw, for home networks which usually don't have a name server, you can put all the computer names with their IP addresses in your /etc/hosts file, and then you can connect to these computers by using their names instead of the IP

---

### Post by Glarbl_Blarbl on 2006-02-19
[QUOTE=Wallakoala]I just kept the default "ubuntu" but now, after reading everyone's interesting computer names, I wish to change it. How would I go about doing that?[/QUOTE]

There are a couple of ways,

1. Use the hostname command like this:
[FONT="Courier New"]sudo hostname *newname*[/FONT]

or
2.edit the [FONT="Courier New"]/etc/hostname file[/FONT].

-
g

### Post by dbott67 on 2006-03-23
I've been running Ubuntu on my old P2-300 laptop for over a year now and started naming it after the version of Ubuntu (Warty, Hoary and Breezy).  Earlier this week, I just ordered a new laptop from Dell (a duo core T2400, with 2 GB RAM, 100 GB HD, ATI Radeon x1400 video, 8x DVD) and was trying to give thought as to what I should name her.

At work, I am doing a very large computer upgrade and am replacing 6 servers & about 100 PCs.  I needed to come up with a naming convention for the new servers (the PCs follow a location-based convention to make them easy to find).  I decided to use the Greek alphabet (alpha, beta, gamma, delta, etc.) for the servers.  In researching some of the names and history of the Greek alphabet, I found that there are a few 'obsolete' letters (stigma, qoppa, digamma, sho, man & sampi).  Considering that my laptop is circa 1999, I decided to rename her 'stigma' (as it's a very fitting name for an IT professional to be using such an antiquated computer).

My new laptop will be called 'omega' (as 'mega'=big and that it's probably the end of the line for new computers for a long time!).  I also renamed my iPAQ 4350 PocketPC to 'omicron' (and fittingly micron=small).  
 
-Dave

---

### Post by kadymae on 2006-03-23
Heh.

At work, one of the Systems people was in my office, trying to figure out what to name the computer in the cubicle next to me. It required a special image and permissions (and it's not the sort of thing she normally does) and she wasn't quite sure which naming convention applied.

A few months back she took me on a tour of the server room and that's when I noticed that a certain class of servers had male LOTR themed names. (Gandalf, Aragorn, Frodo, Bilbo, etc.)

I suggested she name it Galadriel, Arwen, Nienna, or best yet, Rosie Cotton. (It's just a little Gateway desktop)

While she agreed that a good laugh would be had watching the three *nix gurus running around trying to figure out (a) why is there a "girl" server? and (b) where the hell in the building is this box?  and (c) why is it running XP? she took pity on them and didn't do that.

### Post by jorgerivera on 2006-04-28
Well... my first computer with a name was an old 286 running DOS. My dad named it Thomas, as in Thomas Alva Edison.

I changed motherboard and kept the case. First to a Cyrix486 66Mhz, and then to a AMD 5x86 133Mhz and kept the name, so I decided to give names to the cases, even if their minds changed.

I kept using scientist's names, but using the last name, and not the first name as my father did:

Hawking (as in Stephen Hawking): PII 400Mhz 
Einstein (as in... we all know after whom): AthlonXP 1800+ (my sister's box running WinXP)
Volta (as in Alessandro Volta): AthlonXP 2700+ (Ubuntu Dapper)
Ampere (as in Andrè Marie Ampère): in my office AthlonXP 2400+ (Ubuntu Dapper)

Fortunately, there are zillions of good scientists out there to name a big big family of PCs... May the Good Lord make good scientists of us, too!

-----
Jorge Rivera
Cadenux

[LIST]
[*]**fire**, a Sun Ultra 5, 360Mhz UltraSPARC IIi
[*]**blaze**, a self-built low-noise file server in plasma's former shiny blue full tower case (P-III 500Mhz running Debian Stable)
[*]**flame**, a Compaq ProLiant 1850R, 2x P-III 600Mhz, [SIZE="1"]might replace blaze some day, provided I have an appartement with a closet to put the noisy box in[/SIZE]

### Post by arsenic23 on 2006-06-01
This thread is awesome, I just love seeing how other people name their machines.

I have too many compies running in and out of my ownership to only have one method.  So for machines I actually own ( and some I don't ) I name them based on a scheme which I change every year.

My main machine's name is [COLOR="Blue"]Woglinde[/COLOR], and he hails from a year where all my computers where named after [COLOR="DarkRed"]space ships from various fantasy sources[/COLOR].

My Windows/game/Photoshop box is named [COLOR="Blue"]Cliffjumper[/COLOR], and the family's PC is named [COLOR="Blue"]Megatron[/COLOR].  ( [COLOR="DarkRed"]2005 was Transformers year[/COLOR] )

My laptop is named [COLOR="Blue"]Sticky[/COLOR] and my server [COLOR="#0000ff"]ATzilla[/COLOR], because [COLOR="DarkRed"]2006 is physical description year[/COLOR].  The laptop's name is [COLOR="Blue"]Sticky[/COLOR] because I got him after his previous owner dumped a gallon of 7up into him and left him for dead, so the keyboard was sticky untill I happend upon a replacement.  The server gets it's name from being a K7 running on an AT power supply.

The lab I built at work also follows the 2006 theme.  Half of them are generic black/white computers and the other half are sitting in custom painted cases I made durring a particularly slow week at the shop.  We have [COLOR="#0000ff"]BlackKing[/COLOR], [COLOR="#0000ff"]WhiteQueen[/COLOR], [COLOR="#0000ff"]WhitePawn[/COLOR], [COLOR="#0000ff"]OrangeBox[/COLOR], [COLOR="#0000ff"]RedRooster[/COLOR], [COLOR="#0000ff"]Bloo[/COLOR], [COLOR="#0000ff"]Pinky[/COLOR], and [COLOR="#0000ff"]shitball[/COLOR].  The names being pretty much self explanatory.

### Post by der_joachim on 2006-06-02
I've used several hostnames from several contexts over the years. Here's a few:

sickbock (1998-1999): Crappy old Cyrix box in an old server case. 
sickbock (1999-2000): Upgraded my Cyrix to an AMD K6-2 box in aforementioned server case. Sickbock was a comic character by Maarten Toonder. 
dickerdack (1998-2000): my girlfriend's PC, an old IBM. Dickerdack was the mayor in Toonder's books.
cantecler (1998-2000-ish): an old Tulip 486 desktop. Cantecler was the marquis in Toonder's books. Parbleu!

joaputer (2000-2002): A crappy Compaq Presario. Joaputer is short for Joachim's computer.
kimputer (2000-2003): my old K6-2 box, reinstalled for my girlfriend. Guess what her name is. When she moved in with me, she started using eisenmann. 

eisenmann (2002-2006): Another AMD box, albeit with a crappy mobo, eisenmann is German for 'ironman' and refers to the ultra-marathon in the US desert. I thought up the name at a LAN-party I was attending. I had a half marathon planned, but I did not want to miss the LAN-party, so after a long night of gaming I snuck out and ran the race. I ran a PR that day, do the name eisenmann came up and it stuck. :)

remade (2006 - now): When eisenmann died, I had to come up with a new PC and a new name. I was reading China Mieville's 'Iron Council' and Remade seemed like a good name. I salvaged some parts from Eisenmann and 'remade' it into something bigger and stronger. The Remade in Mievilles books are people who were punished and 'remade' into crude cyborg slaves.The PC is an athlon X2 system, on a nForce platform.

### Post by spartas on 2006-06-13
Currently I have four machines, named for Norse mythology (except for one).  

**Asynjur**: my stable Breezy Badger server (very competent file/web/ftp/subversion/dns/ssh DMZ server).  It has no X install, but I didn't install the server CD because I didn't know it existed at the time.  The name reflects its overall purpose.  Intel Xeon box running 5 HDs in RAID5 array.  2GB RAM, Hardware RAID card.

**Athena**: semi-stable KnoppMyth distribution, currently running R5B7 with a Hauppauge 350 card.  My only AMD system.  Sempron 1800+, 320Gb HD, 512 stick of RAM. Not named for Norse mythology.  Occasionally I'll break this while upgrading to a newer version of KnoppMyth, but I like to keep this pretty stable, and not trash my recorded programs DB and filesystem.

**Odin**: My apple (final generation) G4 PowerBook.  1.67Ghz G4, 80Gb HD, and a gig of RAM.  She treats me well--real well.  My everyday stable machine.

**Freyja**:  So named because I ran out of cool sounding names in Norse mythology.  I'm still not sure why I chose this naming scheme, but I do like the names.  Ancient Compaq Presario P3 450Mhz purchased in 1999.  Original hardware, but with 224Mb RAM.  Dapper runs okay on it.  No BIOS support for USB keyboards (makes booting with grub a hassle).  686 Kernel panics on it.  Sigh.

I am currently in the process of building a machine to replace this one.  It's very quirky (and proprietary), and I want something newer to use instead.  This one is my test machine, that I can break and fix and break again.  I'll probably test Edgy on it soon before replacing it.

I used to have a 2003 Dell Insipron, but I sold that to my dad, he is running Fedora on that, the name is Epiphany.  P4m 1.9Ghz with 768 Mb RAM and two batteries.  Fun machine it was, but too bad it's not upgradeable.  That was the main reason I didn't want to keep it around.

### Post by Robb Kidd on 2006-06-14
I have a tendency to use mythological figures, usually the ever popular Greco-Roman batch.  The god-roles map to host-function thing sits nicely in my head.
[LIST]
[*]**janus** - two-faced god of gateways - **firewall/router**
[*]**hermes** - god of trade and communication - **mail servers**, natch
[*]**arachne** - weaver lady turned into a spider - **web servers**
[*]**clotho, lachesis & atropos** - the fates - **LDAP servers**, where accounts are born, prosper and die
[*]**chronos **- god of time - **time servers**, natch
[*]**asklepios** - god of health and medicine - **anti-virus servers**
[*]**hades** - god of death and the underworld - **anti-virus *quarantine* servers**
[*]**minerva/athena** - goddess of wisdom - **file servers**, This naming doesn't quite satisfy.
[*]**vulcan** - god of the forge and fire - the **CD mastering** host
[/LIST]

Two that I've come across on a network that I wish that I'd come up with:
[LIST]
[*]**caduceus** - heraldic staff of Hermes/Mercury - **forward-facing mail gateways**
[*]**talos** - bronze man created by Hephaestus - **spam trap**, This one may require an explanation.  According to one legend, Talos would run laps around the island of Crete, throwing boulders at ships approaching without authorization.  If someone managed to make land fall, Talos would grapple and hold them and then become red-hot.  I love the imagery of fighting spam with rocks and red-hot metal.
[/LIST]

At home, I used to use character names from Terry Pratchett's Discworld series ...
[LIST]
[*]**rincewind** - a main character that gets buffeted about by events - **firewall/router**
[*]**hex** - a magical computer - my **primary desktop**
[*]**hamish** - a seemingly indestructible gnome - my **Toughbook**, now deceased
[/LIST]
... but now use an assortment of the [Discworld's gods]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Discworld_gods") . 
[LIST]
[*]**khefin** - two-faced god of gateways, not unlike Janus - **firewall/router**
[*]**flatulus** - god of the winds - **wireless AP** :D 
[*]**fedecks **- messenger of the gods - the **mail server**
[*]**patina** - goddess of wisdom - my **primary desktop**, formerly hex, running whatever distro of Linux I'm using at the moment.  Patina is a Discworld analog of Athena, but instead of an owl, her symbolic animal is a penguin. 
[*]**ceno** - "a rather liberal god, not big on commandments" - my new **laptop**, which gets blown away and reconfigured all the time 
[*]**astoria** - goddess of love - **wife's desktop**, natch
[/LIST]

192.168.2.3 = lithium
192.168.2.4 = beryllium
etc.

I thought it was a pretty good idea anyway :mrgreen: . . .

### Post by schurtek on 2006-07-24
I have a very twisted way of naming PC's and servers...

At home I have two servers... one runs windows (shudder) 2003 server edition... so I called it Damien (those of you who read horror novels will know that Damien is a common name used for the son of satan.) The other server is running RHEL3.6 so I named it Igore... when I telnet in to that server, the welcome screen says... "Yessss Massssster...."

I have two laptops, one is an old PII that I use to run Getright and BitLord. So it only downloads stuff, nothing else... that one is called Gollum. My newer laptop which is a PIII, is called Frodo. 

My desktop Machines I have two... one is called Benji, as it is the machine my mother uses the most, and it is named after her late dog. The other desktop is running Ubuntu, so I named it Tsotsi.

I am busy building a PC for my girlfriend, so I don't know what I am going to name it yet, but I am working on some ideas, like Gladerail? Yeah, I am a bit of a LOTR freak...

My web server that sits in the US is loving named Mordor.

At the office, I have two servers... the one is called Zeus, as it is the main server and handles everything, except phone calls. That is handled by an Asterisk Server, and that machine is named Hermes, the Messenger of Zeus... each PC in the office is named after the department that it belongs to... Admin1, Admin2, Admin3, DTP-IT1, DTP-IT2, DTP-IT3, GM1, PM1, etc...

**kostkon@kostkon:~$**

instead of

**kostkon@kostkon.ubuntu:~$**

When you combine words with the dot as a *hostname*, only the first word survives; I don't know why. **Anyone!!??**

### Post by dbott67 on 2006-12-08
> **dbbolton said:**
> is it possible to change the name ?

Yes... the name is stored in /etc/hostname.
```
dbott@edgy:/etc$ cat hostname
edgy

```

I think you can edit the file:
```
gksudo gedit /etc/hostname
```
or via GUI:
**SYSTEM > ADMINISTRATION > NETWORKING**
Click on the GENERAL TAB and change the hostname (you may need to reboot)

---

### Post by popch on 2007-07-22
> **KiwiNZ said:**
> Now come folks , naming your computers, now thats crazy, naming your car yes naming your favourite shoes yes but your computer ???:-P:-\"

Why not? I have only one child and gave him a name, even when there was no danger of confusion when speaking about or to him. 

Incidentally, I used to name my computers after planets of our solar system. Then, I ran out of planets and I extended the scheme to any celestial body within the system. Virtual computers get named after continents. When these are done, major landmarks of real or imaginary celestial bodies will come next, I suppose.

### Post by yabbadabbadont on 2007-07-31
> **j.miller565 said:**
> simon-desktop LOL!!!

is there anyway I can change this? lol

```
/home/daffy $ cat /etc/hostname
yoiks
/home/daffy $ grep yoiks /etc/hosts
127.0.1.1       yoiks.and.away  yoiks
/home/daffy $ hostname
yoiks
/home/daffy $ dnsdomainname 
and.away
/home/daffy $ hostname -f
yoiks.and.away

```
The rest is left as an exercise for the student.  :D

### Post by HeavyAl on 2007-08-02
> **j.miller565 said:**
> woah!! how did you get through  every distro?

Well, not EVERY distro .. hehe, I guess that was kind of an exaggeration .. I've been using Linux since the mid 90's so let's see .. started with Slackware, then Red Hat, then Crux .. after that I attempted to get ROCK linux to work but had problems which about the time I noticed Mandrake (later to be mandriva of course) .. then I tried Debian which was cool as far as installing packages but the install I tried back then wanted you to compile everything which was too time consuming for me (a touch of ADD here) ..

At some point I took a hiatus from linux after I got a job as a Delphi dev which meant at the time only Windows .. after I left that gig I took up web development which meant (to me at least) that I needed some kind of personal web server to test junk on and what better web server than apache (70% of the web at the time if IRC) .. sooo .. back to Linux!

Along the way I tried at least a dozen other distros (including that-which-is-not-linux FreeBSD/et al) looking for that one sweet spot - I finally came full circle back to Slackware because it was flexible and development stuff was pretty much all built in. Then one day I saw this odd thing called 'Ubuntu' - decided to give it a shot and was pleasantly surprised at how well structured and thought out it was and it used my favorite desktop environment by default.

So, here I am, typing this up on my Ubuntu driven Thinkpad. No, this particular thinkpad wasn't with me from day one of the journey, but it's sort of the culmination of several years of messing around with these various distros, thus 'chopshop'.

Sorry that was so long, but I figured I'd clear the air in case I sounded like an idiot.

---

### Post by Ozor Mox on 2007-08-21
> **yabbadabbadont said:**
> It has to have a *system name* as you were required to enter one during the installation process...   ;)

In a terminal window, run ```
hostname -f
``` and it will show you the name of your computer.

I find it funny how some people on this thread think that all these people are actually giving a name to their computer, like they would their children or their car! Computers are required to have a name so they can be identified on a network, and whether you are on Windows or Ubuntu, you must have entered a computer name when you installed or set up the operating system.

:lolflag:

Mine are boringly just based on my name followed by "desktop" or "laptop".

### Post by badhat on 2007-08-23
I have two systems, both dual-boot, so four names: fan-club, noisy-boy, blue-moon, silly-girl. The names do have explanations...

The tower system is FAN-CLUB under Linux, or NOISY-BOY under Windows. Both names relate to the high number of fans. There used to be 20 fans: five hard-drive heat sinks with three fans each makes 15, plus upper and lower case fans make 17, plus power supply, CPU and Northbridge makes 20. Recently I changed the Northbridge to passive cooling, so now there are only 19 fans. But I installed switches so the hard-drive fans can be off most of the time; I saw a study recently by Google, which suggests that temperature is not so important for hard drive life.

The laptop is a Toshiba Satellite with a blue tint, so under Linux it is BLUE-MOON. Under Windows it is SILLY-GIRL. (The first syllable of that relates to Cilantro, the disk label of the Windows "C:" hard-drive partition.  Also my wife, who came up with the "noisy-boy" name, is the silly girl... We are both silly, it's a *good *thing. My hard drive partition labels seem to come out of the kitchen: the Linux partition, mounted as X: under Windows, is labeled XLCR, the same letters that are stamped into Excelcior brand Jamaican water crackers. My flash drive labels come from the parts of the mouth and throat: there is a retractable flash drive called Tongue, a dangling one called Uvula, and a thin one called Velum. Of course they are assigned in Windows to drives T:, U: and V:)

Someone might say that giving so much thought to the names of things, shows too much time on my hands. Maybe, but there are times when it makes things easier, to have names that are memorable and that make sense to me.

---

My computer names come from Bungie's Marathon series (originally written for mac during the 90s - the predecessor to Halo -- infact alot of the mythology in Halo ideas continued on from Marathon!)

[COLOR="DarkRed"]**Durandal**[/COLOR] - Main machine, Dell, dual boot, usually running windows (hence the rampancy possibility that is attributed to that name!)
[COLOR="DarkRed"]**Tycho**[/COLOR] - Ubuntu server that will eventually be a gateway & fileserver. 
[COLOR="DarkRed"]**Leela**[/COLOR] - Was my ubuntu toshiba laptop. Died. Just like the Leela of Marathon.

Also my IP addresses are usually the birthyear of a member of the family!.


My new work machine (running fiesty) I've named [COLOR="DarkRed"]**brass-kazoo**[/COLOR] after my trombone! :D

### Post by voided3 on 2007-09-10
I always name mine by CPU type and OS instead of using a name, or if it's a manufactured computer I just use the model number (saves time when installing an OS to just have a fail-safe naming system like that instead of trying to think of something clever...). For example, my desktop w/ an Athlon XP 2500+ is 2500LINUX or 2500XP depending on what OS is booted. 

The exceptions have been Blackie for a black computer case I have, Blinky II (a K6-III computer I have named after my friend's K6-III computer that died; we always called it that because you'd sit there staring at the blinking IDE LED while it tried to load WinXP from its failing hard drive...), and my friend had a HP desktop called the Intel Infadel because it was the only computer in their house that didn't have an AMD processor.

### Post by nweenink on 2007-09-25
I named my computers and servers after ancient figures:
Cleopatra, Nefertite, Cicero, Asterix and VanOldebarneveldt.

I used to do that when I was working as a systems engineer/administrators. At one of my former employers I named all the servers after the cartoon figures from Asterix: Asterix, Obelix, Assurancetourix, Panoramix, etc. :-D
So people would logon to the Abraracourix server and such... People in general liked it, and after a while got acquinted with the names:
"Where did you store that document?"
"Asterix has it, in the Sales/Proposal folder!"

Enjoy!

Nico.

### Post by FrozenFlame22 on 2007-10-05
My LAN is named "Middle Earth" and so everything on the LAN is named appropriately. Computers and printers are places, and individual drives are people.

Modem/router: Palantir

Printer: Bree

Laptop: Minas Tirith
- Hardrive: Faramir

Desktop: Erebor
- Harddrive 1: Gimli
- Harddrive 2: Thorin
- Harddrive 3: Balin
- Harddrive 4: Ori

Flash Drives:
- Bilbo
- Frodo
- Pippin

External Harddrive: Gandalf

Digital Camera: Fangorn
Memory Sticks:
- Treebeard
- Quickbeam
- Leaflock

We've had this naming scheme for quite a while now, so we've built up quite a "graveyard" of retired computers and other hardware:
Edoras
- Théoden
Mirkwood
- Oropher
Lothlórien
- Celeborn (later renamed to Thorin in current desktop)
Moria
- Balin (kept name in current desktop)
- Ori (kept name in current desktop
Printers: Brandywine, Bywater
Flashdrives: Merry, Tom_Bombadil

We figure that it will be a long long time before we run out of names with this naming convention! We were recently given a server with 4 harddrives, and they'll probably get either human or elven names. Right now we're leaning towards "Helm's Deep".

### Post by Simon G Best on 2007-10-29
Well, back in, oh, 1998, I built a 486-based PC out of mostly second-hand bits and pieces, and the like.  It didn't even have a proper PC case, but instead used a crate-like case from an old CP/M micro that itself seemed to have been made out of various bits and pieces (it had had about half an S-100 motherboard - it had literally been sawn in half!).  I named that PC "Cydonia", after the place on Mars with the apparent face.  That PC served me well for a few years.

During Cydonia's life, I bought a second-hand 486 from Cash Converters, to use as a dial-up router thingy, with NAT and a caching nameserver.  I named it "Ophir", after another place on Mars, but I can't remember why (except that it might have had something to do with a gateway, possibly?).

At some point, the friend who'd provided some of the bits for Cydonia asked me if I'd please borrow an IBM RS/6000 that he'd managed to get hold of.  It's because he didn't really have room for it, but had thought it would be a sad waste of a good RS/6000 if it had got dumped.  If I remember correctly, I named it "Arcadia", again after a place on Mars.

In late 2001, a friend gave me his old Celeron-based PC.  It was a few years old, and was in a medium-sized tower case.  As it was my first towering PC, I named it "Olympus", after Olympus Mons, the huge volcano on Mars.  I used that as my main PC until just several weeks ago.

Now I'm using a Dell Inspiron 530n, which came with Ubuntu 7.04 pre-installed.  While I do intend to give it a name, and, again, name it after a place on Mars, I haven't yet got around to choosing a name.  But I think I'll go for somewhere near one of the ice caps, because I think this PC's cool :)

---

### Post by Redeyes_Gambit on 2007-11-05
My laptop is named Silverhawk: 1. because it's silver, and 2. because the hawk portion makes it sound cool ;-) . Since my laptop has Multiple Personality Disorder (lol, a.k.a. multiboot,) AND runs VMs, I have come to name each individual operating system.

[COLOR="Sienna"]**Ubuntu 7.10**[/COLOR]: Flex-Hawk -Because Linux is so flexible. It runs on anything and bends rather than breaks. Also because Compiz creates flexible windows, a pretty unique feature among OSes.

[COLOR="DarkSlateGray"]**Windows Vista**[/COLOR]: Glass-Hawk -Because of Aeroglass, and because Vista constantly breaks on me. Inflexible, rigid, fragile. It fits don't you think?

[COLOR="Blue"]**Windows XP**[/COLOR]: Plastic-Hawk -Because it's cheap (as in poor quality); because it It will break, but is currently more resilient (IMHO) than Vista; and because the Luna interface looks like plastic.

I'm thinking about getting a Macbook at some point, and its OS will be called Platinum-Hawk, since OSX has a somewhat platinum-esque color scheme, and because it's so ridiculously expensive! Also named as such since OSX is reasonably resilient when compared to glassy ole windows Vista and isn't as "cheap" as XP (from what I hear anyway.) At the same time OSX isn't as flexible as Linux (or even XP for that matter), hence OSX is a metal, rather than some sort cool flexible composite material.

### Post by Chelidon on 2007-11-07
> The tower system is FAN-CLUB under Linux, or NOISY-BOY under Windows. Both names relate to the high number of fans. There used to be 20 fans: five hard-drive heat sinks with three fans each makes 15, plus upper and lower case fans make 17, plus power supply, CPU and Northbridge makes 20. Recently I changed the Northbridge to passive cooling, so now there are only 19 fans. But I installed switches so the hard-drive fans can be off most of the time; I saw a study recently by Google, which suggests that temperature is not so important for hard drive life.

Jeez. There's no way I could have that thing on overnight downloading something, I don't think I could sleep.

### Post by stevieb on 2008-01-03
is there any way to change a computer name?  i just grabbed a used one from an xubuntu friend, it's already named "angel".  i'd like to change this without reinstalling.

### Post by mali2297 on 2008-01-03
> **stevieb said:**
> is there any way to change a computer name?  

Go through the menus **System > Administration > Networking > General**, or type
```

gksudo network-admin

```
in the terminal. However, I do not know if you have that in Xubuntu. If not, use the directions from this [link]("http://blog.lxpages.com/2007/03/21/how-to-change-your-hostname/").
> 
Debian based systems use the file /etc/hostname to read the hostname of the system at boot time and set it up using the init script /etc/init.d/hostname.sh.

- Edit /etc/hostname and update to your new hostname, you can then run /etc/init.d/hostname.sh to activiate the change.
- Update your /etc/hosts file to refelect new hostname

You can also use sysctl to change the hostname:

- sysctl kernel.hostname (To read the current hostname)
- sysctl kernel.hostname=NEW_HOSTNAME (to change it)


My computer is called *asparagus*.

### Post by k2t0f12d on 2008-02-27
Originally my desktop was callled ZEUS when it was dual-boot. When I had to return, I reorganized my filesystem, reinstalled Debian and called the result PROMETHEUS (much more appropriate for a GNU/Linux box I thought).  PROMETHEUS is now dual-boot with a built-from-source GNU/Linux I call HERMES.

### Post by LinuxManMikeC on 2008-08-02
Frankenstein - My desktop, which used to be a stock ElitePC, but then I gutted it for a major upgrade.  With the added heat and a graphics card with no fan, I cut two holes in the side for a couple 120mm exhaust fans and drilled holes in one of the 5 1/4 drive bay covers for the two fan control knobs.  I also got a PSU with a second fan on top, so I cut a hole for that too.  Not sure if I'll continue with this upgrade cycle or just get a new case and build a new system.  I kinda like the battered look of it, but there are some sweet cases out there that make me drool and I'd like to go water cooled (which would be hard in the current case).

Phoenix - My IBM Thinkpad 770z that my dad snagged from the junkpile at work several years back.  The hard disk crashed the first time I attempted to install an OS.  After barely getting along with just a 800mb HD (also salvaged from the junk pile) I bought a 40gb drive and it rose from the ashes.

Hive - My server, no idea why I named it this.  Perhaps Borg inspired (I am a bit of a Trekkie).  An old Dell desktop also from the junk pile.

Pegasus - The computer I built for my mom from the leftovers when I created Frankenstein.  She chose the name.  Linux powered, currently Fedora 6 (with a WinXP dual boot), but soon to be Ubuntu 8.04 (and WinXP in VirtualBox).

Tinkerbell - The computer I built for my sister when she left for college.  All hand-picked parts based on what she wanted and how much money she had to spare.  Beautiful computer I must say.  She chose the name.  Linux powered, Fedora 7 x86-64, will eventually be Ubuntu.

### Post by Scunge on 2008-08-26
I used to play a DOS game called *VGA PLanets* and the group I was in had a ship list with names set up by the group, not always the defaults that come with the game. So I named my computers after what they do sounding like the sort of ship it would be in the game.

My disk server is called **ferengi**, after the *Ferengi Tradinger*, the biggest cargo ship in the ship list.

My main working machine, nice and fast, which, being a laptop, is alot less visible than the others (mainly desktops), is **menhunter**, after the *Menhunter Interceptor*, a ship which can travel twice as fast as others and can cloak.

The one the kids use is just an old thing which I've got working enough for them to use, so it's called **sirius**, after the *Sirius Cybernetics*, the most basic cargo ship in our ship list.

The machine I use for "everything else" - it dual boots with Windows XP for those hard-to-find-in-Linux apps and has Hardy Heron on it for me to experiment with (all others have Dapper Drake), is called **wayland**, after the *Wayland Probe*, a ship with hyperdrive used to find out about enemy planets all over the game universe.

And finally, my backup machine, the thing that every good user needs and it just does it's job without any fuss, is called **foundation**, after the *Foundation Freighter*, my most used cargo ship in the games I played.
[img]http://i268.photobucket.com/albums/jj22/Rob_0edab8/Spacer.gif[/img]

### Post by minime80 on 2008-09-17
Okay, I'm definitely going to sound like a nerd now, but oh well. My naming convention stems around the astrotheological origins of ancient mythology. 

The server is named Polaris after the star that many of the characters in mythology dance around. 

Since I tend to gravitate toward a darker theme, I named my domain Hades. 

Since my name is Nick, I named my main laptop Nyx, which also happens to be the greek character from their creation myth that represented the night. 

My smartphone is named Erebus, who was Nyx's brother (both children of the god Chaos), and represented darkness. 

The wifey's laptop is named after Nyx and Erebus's child Nemesis, which I found supremely appropriate (she didn't think so :lolflag:) because, as in Hesiod's *Theogony* "deady Nyx bore Nemesis to afflict mortal men."

PEACE!

### Post by SeanBlader on 2008-10-17
They all get named after Star Wars planets in alphabetical order. Works well, I'm up to Hoth so far. One thing that really worked out well was that when I got my Nokia N95 I needed to name it too since it is a little linux computer, so I named it after one of Naboo's moons. The only letters in the alphabet I'll have to skip are L, X and Z. And when I get to a couple of them I'll have a few options for names depending on what role the system will take. Like Kashyyyk, or Kamino, or Kessel.

So over the years I've had Alderaan, Bespin, Corellia (ubuntu), Dathomir, Endor, Felucia (ubuntu), Geonosis, Hoth. All but the last three are retired. And there's a full list of the rest of the names at [www.starwars.com/databank](www.starwars.com/databank) for me to look up later and decide what to name the next system.

### Post by VorDesigns on 2009-02-07
Working as a consultant; the names I've dealt with have been many and varied.
On my network; all the servers are named after women because women are tougher and more resilient but, when they want to hurt you, it can be a permanent thing.
So, while I won't give out the current productions names, here are past servers
Tessera
Dulcinea
Aldonsa
Ophelia 

Windows Workstations on the other hand are all guys and I like noire detective's names.  The reason for guy names is easy; while sometimes reliable, they screw up all the time.
Marlow (Raymond Chandler)
Cervantes (Bruce Cook)
Mallory (Raymond Chandler)
Deckard (Philip K. Dick)
etc.,

Linux workstations on the other hand usually get names of men from south of the border in homage to Microsoft's active dislike of competition.
Pablo
Pedro
Sanchez
Sanch

Linux servers are still women
Galatea
Sorsha
Amelia

On client sites I've run across everything from the Three Musketteers to names of Italian citys and couple creepy ones like names of mass murderers and the mundane like Server1, Server2.

If I had any big iron or when systems start providing 99.999% up time, I might start naming them after BOLO tanks from Keith Laumer but, there isn't much chance of that happening unless I feel like buying a main frame or old HP/UX system.

### Post by dichtbijzee on 2009-02-12
> **pol666 said:**
> it's for Isaac Asimov really? It's a good idea

"The last question" might be the best Asimov story i know.

from wikipedia: (paraphrased)

Multivac is the name of a fictional supercomputer in many stories by Isaac Asimov from 1955 to 1979. 

In possibly the most famous Multivac story, "The Last Question", two slightly drunken technicians ask Multivac if humanity can reverse the decrease of entropy. Multivac fails, displaying the error message "INSUFFICIENT DATA FOR MEANINGFUL ANSWER". The story continues through many iterations of computer technology, each more powerful and ethereal than the last. Each of these computers is asked the question, and each returns the same response until finally consuming all of the energy of the universe, whereupon an answer is found.

### Post by Mehall on 2009-04-29
> **dragos240 said:**
> Homebrew is my home computer. Modified just the way I like it. The netbook is the name of well..... my netbook. The heap, is the laptop that has been broken every/which/way and still has windows on it, I refuse to use it. There's ways of making a floppy boot a CD for you.

Also, Debian (and others) have floppies which allow you to start netowrking and get everything else needed from the net so you can net-install.

You need 3 floppy discs: boot, root and network.

### Post by ruru on 2009-05-20
I started naming mine alphabetically, like hurricanes. Mac installs get male names, Linux ones female. So my dual booting laptop shows up on the network as 'Darius' or 'Daria' depending on which OS is running. It started off when 'The Brain' (my old PPC bioinformatics workstation) got spelled wrong during setup and ended up as 'Brian'. 'Ariadne' is/was an experiment with building a cluster (she controls the threads in the labyrinth of CPUs?). My current workstation is called 'Grendel' because the only thing that is more powerful is a Beowulf cluster! (To be pedantic, I am aware that this breaks my naming scheme as Grendel is considered to be male although this is an Ubuntu install. I just like the name - and no-one else on the network has it!) 

Hmmm...I guess I could just call them "My_PC" or "Computer1" etc.
But that would be boring.

### Post by SanityKills on 2009-05-22
Ever since I can remember I've always used stars, planets, or constellations since my first handle ever on the internet was "Stargazer". My local network has always been called "Stargate". My hosts are currently:
 
Stargazer
Mars
Electra
Orion
Sirius
Aries
Zeus
Cancer
Neptune
Mercury
 
Now, about 13 years later, I'm rethinking my configuration.
 
At work we use a naming convention with the first two letters stating the city abbreviation, the second two letters state the device type (WS, LP for workstation or laptop, etc.), then the inventory code, then the user's first initials and last name up to 15 characters.
 
It's organized so I'm thinking of the following naming convention for mine as follows:
 
[2 Digit Device Type][4 Digit Brand][8 Digit Model/Number][Sequence Number]. For custom PC's the motherboard brand/model replaces the computer brand/model.
 
So "Stargazer", my main PC, would equate to the following:
 
[COLOR=black][FONT=Arial]WSASUSM2NESLI001[/FONT][/COLOR] 
 
[COLOR=black][FONT=Arial]Although it'll never happen, my logic states that I could eventually have up to 999 workstations utilizing an Asus M2N-E SLI motherboard so I have to allocate for the possibility that all 999 of those should have a unique ID. ;-)[/FONT][/COLOR] 
 
[COLOR=black][FONT=Arial]My new network name will be named "MATRIX" because that's pretty much what a network is.[/FONT][/COLOR]

### Post by hellmitre on 2009-10-15
My laptop (Ubuntu 8.10) is named titan/leviathan, though it was once named cradle. Any of those three is something I may at random switch it to. 

I have a fileserver/torrentbox/webserver/backup system called minus22. It's running 32bit Ubuntu 8.10 on an AMD64 processor; I didn't like the sound of 'minus32' (the relation between the processor bus and the bus the OS was written for) so I named it minus22. I guess I like the alliteration. 
I have four terabytes of storage in it; the first terabyte drive was named 'terror' in a play on words, the second 'tee two' and the third is 't3'. Yep, alliteration.

File server: Miniserver (Dell Vostro A90)

Funny thing, I name my hard drive partitions after storms/natural disasters starting with "T": Tsunami, Torrent, Typhoon, Tornado. Ironically, the 1.5TB external backup drive connected to my file server is a WD Elements, aptly named "Elements."

### Post by Mornedhel on 2010-01-10
My current laptop's name is vega-laptop.

My computers are named $starname-$computer_type, where $starname is the name of a bright star, and $computer_type is "laptop", "desktop" or "server" (haven't had any netbooks or nettops to christen -- yet). Vega is the fifth brightest star in the sky (not counting the Sun), so the next one should be rigel-desktop.

My wireless networks have ESSIDs named after galaxies, so right now I'm connected to "andromeda".

Yeah, I like naming schemes.

### Post by nmsmith on 2010-01-15
Here they are, in order of acquisition:

cruithne - the first PC I named, Athlon 800, now deceased
thrymr - old work laptop
cloanthus - mythtv box *
gaspra - very old phone
praixidike - old second-hand hacking PC
epimetheus - old phone
ananke - current work laptop *
ithaca chasma - old wlan
thebe - usb drive *
himalia - usb drive *
adrastea - netbook *
ogygia chasma - wlan *
nereid - phone *
elara - current fast desktop *

Each is a body in the solar system, chosen by the rigorous method of 'what sounds nice'. The exception is the naming scheme for the wireless ssids, which is surface features on solar system bodies, namely valleys.

I have begun appending "7" to the computer names if they dual boot windows.

Lucy is the second ever brand-new computer I have ever owned.  The first new computer I ever bought was a Vic20 in 1982, and I was only 14, so I wasn't old enough to know how to give names to all the animals back then, but Lucy is my second ever brand-new computer, so she got the name of the first ever primate to apparently leave only one pair of footprints in the mud.
